  3  1 quantifiable positive effect or outcome that is expected to
  3  2 result from implementation of a rule.
  3  3    b.  "Cost" means reasonably identifiable, significant, direct
  3  4 or indirect, economic impact that is expected to result from
  3  5 implementation of and compliance with a rule.
  3  6    c.  "Cost=benefit analysis" means regulatory analysis
  3  7 to provide the public with transparency regarding the
  3  8 cost=effectiveness of a rule, including the economic costs
  3  9 and benefits and the effectiveness weighed by the agency
  3 10 in adopting the rule. "Cost=benefit analysis" includes a
  3 11 comparison of the probable costs and benefits of a rule to the
  3 12 probable costs and benefits of less intrusive or less expensive
  3 13 methods that exist for achieving the purpose of the rule.
  3 14    d.  "Jobs" means private sector employment including
  3 15 self=employment and areas for potential for employment growth.
  3 16    e.  "Jobs impact statement" means a statement that does all
  3 17 of the following:
  3 18    (1)  Identifies the purpose of a rule and the applicable
  3 19 section of the statute that provides specific legal authority
  3 20 for the agency to adopt the rule.
  3 21    (2)  Identifies and describes the cost that the agency
  3 22 anticipates state agencies, local governments, the public, and
  3 23 the regulated entities, including regulated businesses and
  3 24 self=employed individuals, will incur due to implementing and
  3 25 complying with a rule.
  3 26    (3)  Determines whether a rule would have a positive
  3 27 or negative impact on private sector jobs and employment
  3 28 opportunities in Iowa.
  3 29    (4)  Describes and quantifies the nature of the impact a rule
  3 30 will have on private sector jobs and employment opportunities
  3 31 including the categories of jobs and employment opportunities
  3 32 that are affected by the rule, and the number of jobs or
  3 33 potential job opportunities and the regions of the state
  3 34 affected by the rule.
  3 35    (5)  Identifies, where possible, the additional costs to
  4  1 employers per employee due to implementing and complying with
  4  2 a rule.
  4  3    (6)  Includes other relevant analysis requested by the
  4  4 administrative rules coordinator.
  4  5    2.  Prior to implementation of a rule, an agency shall
  4  6 take steps to minimize the adverse impact on jobs and
  4  7 the development of new employment opportunities due to
  4  8 implementation of the rule.
  4  9    3.  An agency shall provide a jobs impact statement to the
  4 10 administrative rules coordinator prior to publication of a
  4 11 notice of intended action or the publication of a rule without
  4 12 notice.
  4 13    4.  The jobs impact statement shall be published as part
  4 14 of the preamble to the notice of rulemaking in the Iowa
  4 15 administrative bulletin, unless the administrative rules
  4 16 coordinator determines that publication of the entire jobs
  4 17 impact statement would be unnecessary or impractical.
  4 18    5.  An agency shall accept comments and information
  4 19 from stakeholders prior to final preparation of the  jobs
  4 20 impact statement. Any concerned private sector employer or
  4 21 self=employed individual, potential employer, potential small
  4 22 business, or member of the public may submit information
  4 23 relating to a jobs impact statement upon a request for
  4 24 information or prior to publication of a notice of intended
  4 25 action or publication of a rule without notice by an agency.
  4 26    6.  If a jobs impact statement is revised after a notice
  4 27 of intended action or a rule without notice is published, the
  4 28 revised jobs impact statement shall be published as part of
  4 29 the preamble to the adopted version of the rule, unless the
  4 30 administrative rules coordinator determines that publication
  4 31 of the entire jobs impact statement would be unnecessary or
  4 32 impractical.
  4 33    7.  The analysis in the jobs impact statement shall give
  4 34 particular weight to jobs in production sectors of the economy
  4 35 which includes the manufacturing and agricultural sectors of
  5  1 the economy and shall include analysis, where applicable, of
  5  2 the impact of the rule on expansion of existing businesses or
  5  3 facilities.
  5  4    8.  The administrative rules coordinator may waive the jobs
  5  5 impact statement requirement for rules proposed on an emergency
  5  6 basis or if unnecessary or impractical.
  5  7    9.  By July 1, 2016, and every five years thereafter, an
  5  8 agency shall prepare a comprehensive jobs impact statement
  5  9 for all of the agency's rules. An agency shall transmit
  5 10 each five=year comprehensive jobs impact statement to the
  5 11 administrative rules coordinator, the administrative rules
  5 12 review committee, and the administrative code editor. The
  5 13 administrative code editor shall publish the statement, or a
  5 14 summary, in the Iowa administrative bulletin.

  3 32 that are affected by the rule, and the number of jobs or
  3 33 potential job opportunities and the regions of the state
  3 34 affected by the rule.
  3 35    (5)  Identifies, where possible, the additional costs to
  4  1 employers per employee due to implementing and complying with
  4  2 a rule.
  4  3    (6)  Includes other relevant analysis requested by the
  4  4 administrative rules coordinator.
  4  5    2.  Prior to implementation of a rule, an agency shall
  4  6 take steps to minimize the adverse impact on jobs and
  4  7 the development of new employment opportunities due to
  4  8 implementation of the rule.
  4  9    3.  An agency shall provide a jobs impact statement to the
  4 10 administrative rules coordinator prior to publication of a
  4 11 notice of intended action or the publication of a rule without
  4 12 notice.
  4 13    4.  The jobs impact statement shall be published as part
  4 14 of the preamble to the notice of rulemaking in the Iowa
  4 15 administrative bulletin, unless the administrative rules
  4 16 coordinator determines that publication of the entire jobs
  4 17 impact statement would be unnecessary or impractical.
  4 18    5.  An agency shall accept comments and information
  4 19 from stakeholders prior to final preparation of the  jobs
  4 20 impact statement. Any concerned private sector employer or
  4 21 self=employed individual, potential employer, potential small
  4 22 business, or member of the public may submit information
  4 23 relating to a jobs impact statement upon a request for
  4 24 information or prior to publication of a notice of intended
  4 25 action or publication of a rule without notice by an agency.
  4 26    6.  If a jobs impact statement is revised after a notice
  4 27 of intended action or a rule without notice is published, the
  4 28 revised jobs impact statement shall be published as part of
  4 29 the preamble to the adopted version of the rule, unless the
  4 30 administrative rules coordinator determines that publication
  4 31 of the entire jobs impact statement would be unnecessary or
  4 32 impractical.
  4 33    7.  The analysis in the jobs impact statement shall give
  4 34 particular weight to jobs in production sectors of the economy
  4 35 which includes the manufacturing and agricultural sectors of
  5  1 the economy and shall include analysis, where applicable, of
  5  2 the impact of the rule on expansion of existing businesses or
  5  3 facilities.
  5  4    8.  The administrative rules coordinator may waive the jobs
  5  5 impact statement requirement for rules proposed on an emergency
  5  6 basis or if unnecessary or impractical.
  5  7    9.  By July 1, 2016, and every five years thereafter, an
  5  8 agency shall prepare a comprehensive jobs impact statement
  5  9 for all of the agency's rules. An agency shall transmit
  5 10 each five=year comprehensive jobs impact statement to the
  5 11 administrative rules coordinator, the administrative rules
  5 12 review committee, and the administrative code editor. The
  5 13 administrative code editor shall publish the statement, or a
  5 14 summary, in the Iowa administrative bulletin.
  5 15    Sec. 5.    3  3    b.  "Cost" means reasonably identifiable, significant, direct
  3  4 or indirect, economic impact that is expected to result from
  3  5 implementation of and compliance with a rule.
  3  6    c.  "Cost=benefit analysis" means regulatory analysis
  3  7 to provide the public with transparency regarding the
  3  8 cost=effectiveness of a rule, including the economic costs
  3  9 and benefits and the effectiveness weighed by the agency
  3 10 in adopting the rule. "Cost=benefit analysis" includes a
  3 11 comparison of the probable costs and benefits of a rule to the
  3 12 probable costs and benefits of less intrusive or less expensive
  3 13 methods that exist for achieving the purpose of the rule.
  3 14    d.  "Jobs" means private sector employment including
  3 15 self=employment and areas for potential for employment growth.
  3 16    e.  "Jobs impact statement" means a statement that does all
  3 17 of the following:
  3 18    (1)  Identifies the purpose of a rule and the applicable
  3 19 section of the statute that provides specific legal authority
  3 20 for the agency to adopt the rule.
  3 21    (2)  Identifies and describes the cost that the agency
  3 22 anticipates state agencies, local governments, the public, and
  3 23 the regulated entities, including regulated businesses and
  3 24 self=employed individuals, will incur due to implementing and
  3 25 complying with a rule.
  3 26    (3)  Determines whether a rule would have a positive
  3 27 or negative impact on private sector jobs and employment
  3 28 opportunities in Iowa.
  3 29    (4)  Describes and quantifies the nature of the impact a rule
  3 30 will have on private sector jobs and employment opportunities
  3 31 including the categories of jobs and employment opportunities
  3 32 that are affected by the rule, and the number of jobs or
  3 33 potential job opportunities and the regions of the state
  3 34 affected by the rule.
  3 35    (5)  Identifies, where possible, the additional costs to
  4  1 employers per employee due to implementing and complying with
  4  2 a rule.

  3 11 comparison of the probable costs and benefits of a rule to the
  3 12 probable costs and benefits of less intrusive or less expensive
  3 13 methods that exist for achieving the purpose of the rule.
  3 14    d.  "Jobs" means private sector employment including
  3 15 self=employment and areas for potential for employment growth.
  3 16    e.  "Jobs impact statement" means a statement that does all
  3 17 of the following:
  3 18    (1)  Identifies the purpose of a rule and the applicable
  3 19 section of the statute that provides specific legal authority
  3 20 for the agency to adopt the rule.
  3 21    (2)  Identifies and describes the cost that the agency
  3 22 anticipates state agencies, local governments, the public, and
  3 23 the regulated entities, including regulated businesses and
  3 24 self=employed individuals, will incur due to implementing and
  3 25 complying with a rule.
  3 26    (3)  Determines whether a rule would have a positive
  3 27 or negative impact on private sector jobs and employment
  3 28 opportunities in Iowa.
  3 29    (4)  Describes and quantifies the nature of the impact a rule
  3 30 will have on private sector jobs and employment opportunities
  3 31 including the categories of jobs and employment opportunities
  3 32 that are affected by the rule, and the number of jobs or
  3 33 potential job opportunities and the regions of the state
  3 34 affected by the rule.
  3 35    (5)  Identifies, where possible, the additional costs to
  4  1 employers per employee due to implementing and complying with
  4  2 a rule.
  4  3    (6)  Includes other relevant analysis requested by the
  4  4 administrative rules coordinator.
  4  5    2.  Prior to implementation of a rule, an agency shall
  4  6 take steps to minimize the adverse impact on jobs and
  4  7 the development of new employment opportunities due to
  4  8 implementation of the rule.
  4  9    3.  An agency shall provide a jobs impact statement to the
  4 10 administrative rules coordinator prior to publication of a
  4 11 notice of intended action or the publication of a rule without
  4 12 notice.
  4 13    4.  The jobs impact statement shall be published as part
  4 14 of the preamble to the notice of rulemaking in the Iowa
  4 15 administrative bulletin, unless the administrative rules
  4 16 coordinator determines that publication of the entire jobs
  4 17 impact statement would be unnecessary or impractical.
  4 18    5.  An agency shall accept comments and information
  4 19 from stakeholders prior to final preparation of the  jobs
  4 20 impact statement. Any concerned private sector employer or
  4 21 self=employed individual, potential employer, potential small
  4 22 business, or member of the public may submit information
  4 23 relating to a jobs impact statement upon a request for
  4 24 information or prior to publication of a notice of intended
  4 25 action or publication of a rule without notice by an agency.
  4 26    6.  If a jobs impact statement is revised after a notice
  4 27 of intended action or a rule without notice is published, the
  4 28 revised jobs impact statement shall be published as part of
  4 29 the preamble to the adopted version of the rule, unless the
  4 30 administrative rules coordinator determines that publication
  4 31 of the entire jobs impact statement would be unnecessary or
  4 32 impractical.
  4 33    7.  The analysis in the jobs impact statement shall give
  4 34 particular weight to jobs in production sectors of the economy
  4 35 which includes the manufacturing and agricultural sectors of
  5  1 the economy and shall include analysis, where applicable, of
  5  2 the impact of the rule on expansion of existing businesses or
  5  3 facilities.
  5  4    8.  The administrative rules coordinator may waive the jobs
  5  5 impact statement requirement for rules proposed on an emergency
  5  6 basis or if unnecessary or impractical.
  5  7    9.  By July 1, 2016, and every five years thereafter, an
  5  8 agency shall prepare a comprehensive jobs impact statement
  5  9 for all of the agency's rules. An agency shall transmit
  5 10 each five=year comprehensive jobs impact statement to the
  5 11 administrative rules coordinator, the administrative rules
  5 12 review committee, and the administrative code editor. The
  5 13 administrative code editor shall publish the statement, or a
  5 14 summary, in the Iowa administrative bulletin.

  4  7 the development of new employment opportunities due to
  4  8 implementation of the rule.
  4  9    3.  An agency shall provide a jobs impact statement to the
  4 10 administrative rules coordinator prior to publication of a
  4 11 notice of intended action or the publication of a rule without
  4 12 notice.
  4 13    4.  The jobs impact statement shall be published as part
  4 14 of the preamble to the notice of rulemaking in the Iowa
  4 15 administrative bulletin, unless the administrative rules
  4 16 coordinator determines that publication of the entire jobs
  4 17 impact statement would be unnecessary or impractical.
  4 18    5.  An agency shall accept comments and information
  4 19 from stakeholders prior to final preparation of the  jobs
  4 20 impact statement. Any concerned private sector employer or
  4 21 self=employed individual, potential employer, potential small
  4 22 business, or member of the public may submit information
  4 23 relating to a jobs impact statement upon a request for
  4 24 information or prior to publication of a notice of intended
  4 25 action or publication of a rule without notice by an agency.
  4 26    6.  If a jobs impact statement is revised after a notice
  4 27 of intended action or a rule without notice is published, the
  4 28 revised jobs impact statement shall be published as part of
  4 29 the preamble to the adopted version of the rule, unless the
  4 30 administrative rules coordinator determines that publication
  4 31 of the entire jobs impact statement would be unnecessary or
  4 32 impractical.
  4 33    7.  The analysis in the jobs impact statement shall give
  4 34 particular weight to jobs in production sectors of the economy
  4 35 which includes the manufacturing and agricultural sectors of
  5  1 the economy and shall include analysis, where applicable, of
  5  2 the impact of the rule on expansion of existing businesses or
  5  3 facilities.
  5  4    8.  The administrative rules coordinator may waive the jobs
  5  5 impact statement requirement for rules proposed on an emergency
  5  6 basis or if unnecessary or impractical.
  5  7    9.  By July 1, 2016, and every five years thereafter, an
  5  8 agency shall prepare a comprehensive jobs impact statement
  5  9 for all of the agency's rules. An agency shall transmit
  5 10 each five=year comprehensive jobs impact statement to the
  5 11 administrative rules coordinator, the administrative rules
  5 12 review committee, and the administrative code editor. The
  5 13 administrative code editor shall publish the statement, or a
  5 14 summary, in the Iowa administrative bulletin.

  4 31 of the entire jobs impact statement would be unnecessary or
  4 32 impractical.
  4 33    7.  The analysis in the jobs impact statement shall give
  4 34 particular weight to jobs in production sectors of the economy
  4 35 which includes the manufacturing and agricultural sectors of
  5  1 the economy and shall include analysis, where applicable, of
  5  2 the impact of the rule on expansion of existing businesses or
  5  3 facilities.
  5  4    8.  The administrative rules coordinator may waive the jobs
  5  5 impact statement requirement for rules proposed on an emergency
  5  6 basis or if unnecessary or impractical.
  5  7    9.  By July 1, 2016, and every five years thereafter, an
  5  8 agency shall prepare a comprehensive jobs impact statement
  5  9 for all of the agency's rules. An agency shall transmit
  5 10 each five=year comprehensive jobs impact statement to the
  5 11 administrative rules coordinator, the administrative rules
  5 12 review committee, and the administrative code editor. The
  5 13 administrative code editor shall publish the statement, or a
  5 14 summary, in the Iowa administrative bulletin.
  5 15    Sec. 5.    3 25 complying with a rule.
  3 26    (3)  Determines whether a rule would have a positive
  3 27 or negative impact on private sector jobs and employment
  3 28 opportunities in Iowa.
  3 29    (4)  Describes and quantifies the nature of the impact a rule
  3 30 will have on private sector jobs and employment opportunities
  3 31 including the categories of jobs and employment opportunities
  3 32 that are affected by the rule, and the number of jobs or
  3 33 potential job opportunities and the regions of the state
  3 34 affected by the rule.
  3 35    (5)  Identifies, where possible, the additional costs to
  4  1 employers per employee due to implementing and complying with
  4  2 a rule.
  4  3    (6)  Includes other relevant analysis requested by the
  4  4 administrative rules coordinator.
  4  5    2.  Prior to implementation of a rule, an agency shall
  4  6 take steps to minimize the adverse impact on jobs and
  4  7 the development of new employment opportunities due to
  4  8 implementation of the rule.
  4  9    3.  An agency shall provide a jobs impact statement to the
  4 10 administrative rules coordinator prior to publication of a
  4 11 notice of intended action or the publication of a rule without
  4 12 notice.
  4 13    4.  The jobs impact statement shall be published as part
  4 14 of the preamble to the notice of rulemaking in the Iowa
  4 15 administrative bulletin, unless the administrative rules
  4 16 coordinator determines that publication of the entire jobs
  4 17 impact statement would be unnecessary or impractical.
  4 18    5.  An agency shall accept comments and information
  4 19 from stakeholders prior to final preparation of the  jobs
  4 20 impact statement. Any concerned private sector employer or
  4 21 self=employed individual, potential employer, potential small
  4 22 business, or member of the public may submit information
  4 23 relating to a jobs impact statement upon a request for
  4 24 information or prior to publication of a notice of intended
  4 25 action or publication of a rule without notice by an agency.
  4 26    6.  If a jobs impact statement is revised after a notice
  4 27 of intended action or a rule without notice is published, the
  4 28 revised jobs impact statement shall be published as part of
  4 29 the preamble to the adopted version of the rule, unless the
  4 30 administrative rules coordinator determines that publication
  4 31 of the entire jobs impact statement would be unnecessary or
  4 32 impractical.

  4 17 impact statement would be unnecessary or impractical.
  4 18    5.  An agency shall accept comments and information
  4 19 from stakeholders prior to final preparation of the  jobs
  4 20 impact statement. Any concerned private sector employer or
  4 21 self=employed individual, potential employer, potential small
  4 22 business, or member of the public may submit information
  4 23 relating to a jobs impact statement upon a request for
  4 24 information or prior to publication of a notice of intended
  4 25 action or publication of a rule without notice by an agency.
  4 26    6.  If a jobs impact statement is revised after a notice
  4 27 of intended action or a rule without notice is published, the
  4 28 revised jobs impact statement shall be published as part of
  4 29 the preamble to the adopted version of the rule, unless the
  4 30 administrative rules coordinator determines that publication
  4 31 of the entire jobs impact statement would be unnecessary or
  4 32 impractical.
  4 33    7.  The analysis in the jobs impact statement shall give
  4 34 particular weight to jobs in production sectors of the economy
  4 35 which includes the manufacturing and agricultural sectors of
  5  1 the economy and shall include analysis, where applicable, of
  5  2 the impact of the rule on expansion of existing businesses or
  5  3 facilities.
  5  4    8.  The administrative rules coordinator may waive the jobs
  5  5 impact statement requirement for rules proposed on an emergency
  5  6 basis or if unnecessary or impractical.
  5  7    9.  By July 1, 2016, and every five years thereafter, an
  5  8 agency shall prepare a comprehensive jobs impact statement
  5  9 for all of the agency's rules. An agency shall transmit
  5 10 each five=year comprehensive jobs impact statement to the
  5 11 administrative rules coordinator, the administrative rules
  5 12 review committee, and the administrative code editor. The
  5 13 administrative code editor shall publish the statement, or a
  5 14 summary, in the Iowa administrative bulletin.

  4 23 relating to a jobs impact statement upon a request for
  4 24 information or prior to publication of a notice of intended
  4 25 action or publication of a rule without notice by an agency.
  4 26    6.  If a jobs impact statement is revised after a notice
  4 27 of intended action or a rule without notice is published, the
  4 28 revised jobs impact statement shall be published as part of
  4 29 the preamble to the adopted version of the rule, unless the
  4 30 administrative rules coordinator determines that publication
  4 31 of the entire jobs impact statement would be unnecessary or
  4 32 impractical.
  4 33    7.  The analysis in the jobs impact statement shall give
  4 34 particular weight to jobs in production sectors of the economy
  4 35 which includes the manufacturing and agricultural sectors of
  5  1 the economy and shall include analysis, where applicable, of
  5  2 the impact of the rule on expansion of existing businesses or
  5  3 facilities.

  5  5 impact statement requirement for rules proposed on an emergency
  5  6 basis or if unnecessary or impractical.

  5 15    Sec. 5.    5 14 summary, in the Iowa administrative bulletin.
  5 15    Sec. 5.    5 15    Sec. 5.    5 16    1.  An agency shall create a negotiated rulemaking group if
  5 17 required by statute. An agency may, on its own motion or upon
  5 18 request, create a negotiated rulemaking group if the agency
  5 19 determines that a negotiated rulemaking group can adequately
  5 20 represent the interests that will be significantly affected by
  5 21 a draft rule proposal and that it is feasible and appropriate
  5 22 in the particular rulemaking. Notice of the creation of a
  5 23 negotiated rulemaking group shall be published in the Iowa
  5 24 administrative bulletin. Upon establishing a negotiated
  5 25 rulemaking group, the agency shall also specify a time frame
  5 26 for group deliberations.
  5 27    2.  Unless otherwise provided by statute, the agency shall
  5 28 appoint a sufficient number of members to the group so that
  5 29 a fair cross section of interests and opinions regarding the
  5 30 draft rule proposal is represented. One person shall be
  5 31 appointed to represent the agency. The group shall select its
  5 32 own chairperson and adopt its rules of procedure. All meetings
  5 33 of the group shall be open to the public. A majority of the
  5 34 membership constitutes a quorum. Members shall not receive
  5 35 any per diem payment but shall be reimbursed for all necessary
  6  1 expenses. Any vacancy shall be filled in the same manner as
  6  2 the initial appointment.
  6  3    3.  Prior to the publication of a notice of intended action,
  6  4 the group shall consider the terms or substance of the rule
  6  5 proposed by the agency and shall attempt to reach a consensus
  6  6 on the advisability of adopting the draft rule proposal.
  6  7    4.  If a group reaches a consensus on a draft rule proposal,
  6  8 the group shall transmit to the agency a report containing the
  6  9 consensus on the draft rule proposal. If the group does not
  6 10 reach a consensus on a draft rule proposal within the specified
  6 11 time frame, the group shall transmit to the agency a report
  6 12 stating that inability to reach a consensus and specifying any
  6 13 areas in which the group reached a consensus. The group may
  6 14 include in a report any other information, recommendations,
  6 15 or materials that the group considers appropriate. Any group
  6 16 member may include as an addendum to the report additional
  6 17 information, recommendations, or materials. A report issued
  6 18 under this subsection shall not be considered final agency
  6 19 action for purposes of judicial review.
  6 20    5.  Unless otherwise provided by statute, following
  6 21 consideration of a draft rule proposal by a negotiated
  6 22 rulemaking group, the agency may commence rulemaking as
  6 23 provided in section 17A.4. The group is automatically
  6 24 abolished upon the agency's adoption of the rule pursuant to
  6 25 the provisions of section 17A.5.

  6 11 time frame, the group shall transmit to the agency a report
  6 12 stating that inability to reach a consensus and specifying any
  6 13 areas in which the group reached a consensus. The group may
  6 14 include in a report any other information, recommendations,
  6 15 or materials that the group considers appropriate. Any group
  6 16 member may include as an addendum to the report additional
  6 17 information, recommendations, or materials. A report issued
  6 18 under this subsection shall not be considered final agency
  6 19 action for purposes of judicial review.
  6 20    5.  Unless otherwise provided by statute, following
  6 21 consideration of a draft rule proposal by a negotiated
  6 22 rulemaking group, the agency may commence rulemaking as
  6 23 provided in section 17A.4. The group is automatically
  6 24 abolished upon the agency's adoption of the rule pursuant to
  6 25 the provisions of section 17A.5.

  8  3 an agency charged with the implementation of a federal statute,
  8  4 regulation, or policy shall not implement the federal statute,
  8  5 regulation, or policy in a manner that exceeds the specific
  8  6 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or policy.
  8  7    2.  Any portion of an agency rule or policy that implements
  8  8 a federal statute, regulation, or policy and that exceeds the
  8  9 specific requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or
  8 10 policy is automatically superseded by the specific requirements
  8 11 of that federal statute, regulation, or policy.
  8 12    Sec. 8.  ENVIRONMENTAL REGULATION STUDY.
  8 13    1.  The legislative council, in consultation with the
  8 14 department of natural resources, shall establish a study to
  8 15 analyze the projected financial effects of current and proposed
  8 16 United States environmental protection agency regulations and
  8 17 Iowa department of natural resources rules on Iowa cities over
  8 18 a ten=year period.
  8 19    2.  The study should include an analysis of projected
  8 20 financial costs of such regulations and rules on a hypothetical
  8 21 small Iowa community, medium=sized Iowa community, and large
  8 22 Iowa community.
  8 23    3.  The study shall be concluded by June 30, 2016, and a
  8 24 report shall be provided to the members of the general assembly
  8 25 and to the governor.
  8 26    Sec. 9.  EFFECTIVE DATE.  The section of this Act amending
  8 27 section 17A.7, subsection 2, takes effect July 1, 2017.
  8 28                           EXPLANATION
  8 29 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  8 30 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  8 31    This bill relates to the review of administrative rules and
  8 32 the rulemaking process.
  8 33    CITIZENS' ADVISORY COMMITTEE.  The bill requires that the
  8 34 administrative rules coordinator create a citizens' committee,
  8 35 to advise the administrative rules coordinator on rulemaking
  9  1 issues. The members of the committee shall not be paid a per
  9  2 diem but shall be reimbursed for travel expenses.
  9  3    RULEMAKING HEARINGS THROUGHOUT STATE.  The bill requires
  9  4 administrative agencies, to the extent practicable, to hold
  9  5 rulemaking hearings in varied locations throughout the state
  9  6 via the Iowa communications network or other electronic means
  9  7 and provides that a hearing must be held in a particular city
  9  8 or county when 25 interested persons from that city or county
  9  9 make the request.
  9 10    PRINCIPAL REASONS FOR AND AGAINST RULE.  The bill requires
  9 11 that every adopted rule must be accompanied by a concise
  9 12 statement of the principal reasons for and against the rule
  9 13 adopted. Under current law such a statement is only provided
  9 14 on request.
  9 15    JOBS IMPACT STATEMENTS.  The bill requires that every
  9 16 proposed rule under a notice of intended action or publication
  9 17 without notice contain a jobs impact statement which outlines
  9 18 the purpose and statutory authority of the rule and analyzes
  9 19 and sets out in detail the impact of the proposed rule on state
  9 20 agencies, local governments, the public, and the regulated
  9 21 entities, including regulated businesses and self=employed
  9 22 individuals affected by the rule. The statement must also
  9 23 determine whether a proposed rule would have a positive
  9 24 or negative impact on private sector jobs and employment
  9 25 opportunities.
  9 26    Commencing July 1, 2016, and every five years thereafter,
  9 27 each agency shall prepare a jobs impact statement for all of
  9 28 the agency's rules. The statement must be published in the
  9 29 Iowa administrative bulletin.
  9 30    As part of this requirement, an agency is required to
  9 31 takes steps to minimize the adverse impact on jobs and the
  9 32 development of new employment opportunities before proposing
  9 33 a rule.
  9 34    The administrative rules coordinator may waive the jobs
  9 35 impact statement requirement for emergency=filed rules or if
 10  1 unnecessary or impractical.
 10  2    NEGOTIATED RULEMAKING GROUPS.  If required by statute,
 10  3 this bill requires an agency to create an ad hoc negotiated
 10  4 rulemaking group to review draft rule proposals prior to
 10  5 commencing a rulemaking proceeding. Where a statute does not
 10  6 require this review, the bill allows an agency to create such
 10  7 a review group. Members are appointed by the agency and the
 10  8 composition must adequately represent a fair cross section of
 10  9 interests and opinions regarding the rule. Once such a group
 10 10 is created, the agency may only commence rulemaking after the
 10 11 group has considered the draft rule proposal in question. This
 10 12 provision is based on similar provisions found in the federal
 10 13 Administrative Procedures Act.
 10 14    FIVE=YEAR CYCLE OF AGENCY REVIEW OF RULES.  Current
 10 15 law requires that each state agency review all of its
 10 16 administrative rules on a five=year cycle. The bill provides
 10 17 additional procedures and criteria for such reviews.
 10 18    FEDERAL LAW IMPLEMENTATION.  The bill also provides that
 10 19 state implementation of a federal statute, regulation,
 10 20 or policy by a state agency shall not exceed the specific
 10 21 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or
 10 22 policy, except as specifically allowed by state law. Any
 10 23 portion of a state rule or policy that implements a federal
 10 24 statute, regulation, or policy and that exceeds the specific
 10 25 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or policy is
 10 26 automatically superseded by the specific requirements of that
 10 27 federal statute, regulation, or policy.
 10 28    ENVIRONMENTAL RULES STUDY.  The bill provides that the
 10 29 legislative council, in consultation with the department of
 10 30 natural resources, shall establish a study to analyze the
 10 31 projected financial effects of current and proposed United
 10 32 States environmental protection agency regulations and Iowa
 10 33 department of natural resources rules on Iowa cities over a
 10 34 10=year period. The report of the study must be completed by
 10 35 June 30, 2016.
 11  1 EFFECTIVE DATE.  The provision of the bill relating to state
 11  2 agency review of administrative rules on a five=year cycle
 11  3 takes effect July 1, 2017.
       LSB 1809XS (3) 86

  8  5 regulation, or policy in a manner that exceeds the specific
  8  6 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or policy.
  8  7    2.  Any portion of an agency rule or policy that implements
  8  8 a federal statute, regulation, or policy and that exceeds the
  8  9 specific requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or
  8 10 policy is automatically superseded by the specific requirements
  8 11 of that federal statute, regulation, or policy.
  8 12    Sec. 8.  ENVIRONMENTAL REGULATION STUDY.
  8 13    1.  The legislative council, in consultation with the
  8 14 department of natural resources, shall establish a study to
  8 15 analyze the projected financial effects of current and proposed
  8 16 United States environmental protection agency regulations and
  8 17 Iowa department of natural resources rules on Iowa cities over
  8 18 a ten=year period.
  8 19    2.  The study should include an analysis of projected
  8 20 financial costs of such regulations and rules on a hypothetical
  8 21 small Iowa community, medium=sized Iowa community, and large
  8 22 Iowa community.
  8 23    3.  The study shall be concluded by June 30, 2016, and a
  8 24 report shall be provided to the members of the general assembly
  8 25 and to the governor.
  8 26    Sec. 9.  EFFECTIVE DATE.  The section of this Act amending
  8 27 section 17A.7, subsection 2, takes effect July 1, 2017.

 10 10 is created, the agency may only commence rulemaking after the
 10 11 group has considered the draft rule proposal in question. This
 10 12 provision is based on similar provisions found in the federal
 10 13 Administrative Procedures Act.
 10 14    FIVE=YEAR CYCLE OF AGENCY REVIEW OF RULES.  Current
 10 15 law requires that each state agency review all of its
 10 16 administrative rules on a five=year cycle. The bill provides
 10 17 additional procedures and criteria for such reviews.
 10 18    FEDERAL LAW IMPLEMENTATION.  The bill also provides that
 10 19 state implementation of a federal statute, regulation,
 10 20 or policy by a state agency shall not exceed the specific
 10 21 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or
 10 22 policy, except as specifically allowed by state law. Any
 10 23 portion of a state rule or policy that implements a federal
 10 24 statute, regulation, or policy and that exceeds the specific
 10 25 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or policy is
 10 26 automatically superseded by the specific requirements of that
 10 27 federal statute, regulation, or policy.
 10 28    ENVIRONMENTAL RULES STUDY.  The bill provides that the
 10 29 legislative council, in consultation with the department of
 10 30 natural resources, shall establish a study to analyze the
 10 31 projected financial effects of current and proposed United
 10 32 States environmental protection agency regulations and Iowa
 10 33 department of natural resources rules on Iowa cities over a
 10 34 10=year period. The report of the study must be completed by
 10 35 June 30, 2016.
 11  1 EFFECTIVE DATE.  The provision of the bill relating to state
 11  2 agency review of administrative rules on a five=year cycle
 11  3 takes effect July 1, 2017.
       LSB 1809XS (3) 86
       je/rj
  8  5 regulation, or policy in a manner that exceeds the specific
  8  6 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or policy.
  8  7    2.  Any portion of an agency rule or policy that implements
  8  8 a federal statute, regulation, or policy and that exceeds the
  8  9 specific requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or
  8 10 policy is automatically superseded by the specific requirements
  8 11 of that federal statute, regulation, or policy.
  8 12    Sec. 8.  ENVIRONMENTAL REGULATION STUDY.
  8 13    1.  The legislative council, in consultation with the
  8 14 department of natural resources, shall establish a study to
  8 15 analyze the projected financial effects of current and proposed
  8 16 United States environmental protection agency regulations and
  8 17 Iowa department of natural resources rules on Iowa cities over
  8 18 a ten=year period.
  8 19    2.  The study should include an analysis of projected
  8 20 financial costs of such regulations and rules on a hypothetical
  8 21 small Iowa community, medium=sized Iowa community, and large
  8 22 Iowa community.
  8 23    3.  The study shall be concluded by June 30, 2016, and a
  8 24 report shall be provided to the members of the general assembly
  8 25 and to the governor.
  8 26    Sec. 9.  EFFECTIVE DATE.  The section of this Act amending
  8 27 section 17A.7, subsection 2, takes effect July 1, 2017.
  8 28                           EXPLANATION
  8 29 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  8 30 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  8 31    This bill relates to the review of administrative rules and
  8 32 the rulemaking process.
  8 33    CITIZENS' ADVISORY COMMITTEE.  The bill requires that the
  8 34 administrative rules coordinator create a citizens' committee,
  8 35 to advise the administrative rules coordinator on rulemaking
  9  1 issues. The members of the committee shall not be paid a per
  9  2 diem but shall be reimbursed for travel expenses.
  9  3    RULEMAKING HEARINGS THROUGHOUT STATE.  The bill requires
  9  4 administrative agencies, to the extent practicable, to hold
  9  5 rulemaking hearings in varied locations throughout the state
  9  6 via the Iowa communications network or other electronic means
  9  7 and provides that a hearing must be held in a particular city
  9  8 or county when 25 interested persons from that city or county
  9  9 make the request.
  9 10    PRINCIPAL REASONS FOR AND AGAINST RULE.  The bill requires
  9 11 that every adopted rule must be accompanied by a concise
  9 12 statement of the principal reasons for and against the rule
  9 13 adopted. Under current law such a statement is only provided
  9 14 on request.
  9 15    JOBS IMPACT STATEMENTS.  The bill requires that every
  9 16 proposed rule under a notice of intended action or publication
  9 17 without notice contain a jobs impact statement which outlines
  9 18 the purpose and statutory authority of the rule and analyzes
  9 19 and sets out in detail the impact of the proposed rule on state
  9 20 agencies, local governments, the public, and the regulated
  9 21 entities, including regulated businesses and self=employed
  9 22 individuals affected by the rule. The statement must also
  9 23 determine whether a proposed rule would have a positive
  9 24 or negative impact on private sector jobs and employment
  9 25 opportunities.
  9 26    Commencing July 1, 2016, and every five years thereafter,
  9 27 each agency shall prepare a jobs impact statement for all of
  9 28 the agency's rules. The statement must be published in the
  9 29 Iowa administrative bulletin.
  9 30    As part of this requirement, an agency is required to
  9 31 takes steps to minimize the adverse impact on jobs and the
  9 32 development of new employment opportunities before proposing
  9 33 a rule.
  9 34    The administrative rules coordinator may waive the jobs
  9 35 impact statement requirement for emergency=filed rules or if
 10  1 unnecessary or impractical.
 10  2    NEGOTIATED RULEMAKING GROUPS.  If required by statute,
 10  3 this bill requires an agency to create an ad hoc negotiated
 10  4 rulemaking group to review draft rule proposals prior to
 10  5 commencing a rulemaking proceeding. Where a statute does not
 10  6 require this review, the bill allows an agency to create such
 10  7 a review group. Members are appointed by the agency and the
 10  8 composition must adequately represent a fair cross section of
 10  9 interests and opinions regarding the rule. Once such a group
 10 10 is created, the agency may only commence rulemaking after the
 10 11 group has considered the draft rule proposal in question. This
 10 12 provision is based on similar provisions found in the federal
 10 13 Administrative Procedures Act.
 10 14    FIVE=YEAR CYCLE OF AGENCY REVIEW OF RULES.  Current
 10 15 law requires that each state agency review all of its
 10 16 administrative rules on a five=year cycle. The bill provides
 10 17 additional procedures and criteria for such reviews.
 10 18    FEDERAL LAW IMPLEMENTATION.  The bill also provides that
 10 19 state implementation of a federal statute, regulation,
 10 20 or policy by a state agency shall not exceed the specific
 10 21 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or
 10 22 policy, except as specifically allowed by state law. Any
 10 23 portion of a state rule or policy that implements a federal
 10 24 statute, regulation, or policy and that exceeds the specific
 10 25 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or policy is
 10 26 automatically superseded by the specific requirements of that
 10 27 federal statute, regulation, or policy.
 10 28    ENVIRONMENTAL RULES STUDY.  The bill provides that the
 10 29 legislative council, in consultation with the department of
 10 30 natural resources, shall establish a study to analyze the
 10 31 projected financial effects of current and proposed United
 10 32 States environmental protection agency regulations and Iowa
 10 33 department of natural resources rules on Iowa cities over a
 10 34 10=year period. The report of the study must be completed by
 10 35 June 30, 2016.
 11  1 EFFECTIVE DATE.  The provision of the bill relating to state
 11  2 agency review of administrative rules on a five=year cycle
 11  3 takes effect July 1, 2017.
       LSB 1809XS (3) 86
       je/rj
  8  6 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or policy.
  8  7    2.  Any portion of an agency rule or policy that implements
  8  8 a federal statute, regulation, or policy and that exceeds the
  8  9 specific requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or
  8 10 policy is automatically superseded by the specific requirements
  8 11 of that federal statute, regulation, or policy.
  8 12    Sec. 8.  ENVIRONMENTAL REGULATION STUDY.
  8 13    1.  The legislative council, in consultation with the
  8 14 department of natural resources, shall establish a study to
  8 15 analyze the projected financial effects of current and proposed
  8 16 United States environmental protection agency regulations and
  8 17 Iowa department of natural resources rules on Iowa cities over
  8 18 a ten=year period.
  8 19    2.  The study should include an analysis of projected
  8 20 financial costs of such regulations and rules on a hypothetical
  8 21 small Iowa community, medium=sized Iowa community, and large
  8 22 Iowa community.
  8 23    3.  The study shall be concluded by June 30, 2016, and a
  8 24 report shall be provided to the members of the general assembly
  8 25 and to the governor.
  8 26    Sec. 9.  EFFECTIVE DATE.  The section of this Act amending
  8 27 section 17A.7, subsection 2, takes effect July 1, 2017.

 10 24 statute, regulation, or policy and that exceeds the specific
 10 25 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or policy is
 10 26 automatically superseded by the specific requirements of that
 10 27 federal statute, regulation, or policy.
 10 28    ENVIRONMENTAL RULES STUDY.  The bill provides that the
 10 29 legislative council, in consultation with the department of
 10 30 natural resources, shall establish a study to analyze the
 10 31 projected financial effects of current and proposed United
 10 32 States environmental protection agency regulations and Iowa
 10 33 department of natural resources rules on Iowa cities over a
 10 34 10=year period. The report of the study must be completed by
 10 35 June 30, 2016.
 11  1 EFFECTIVE DATE.  The provision of the bill relating to state
 11  2 agency review of administrative rules on a five=year cycle
 11  3 takes effect July 1, 2017.
       LSB 1809XS (3) 86
       je/rj
  8 10 policy is automatically superseded by the specific requirements
  8 11 of that federal statute, regulation, or policy.
  8 12    Sec. 8.  ENVIRONMENTAL REGULATION STUDY.
  8 13    1.  The legislative council, in consultation with the
  8 14 department of natural resources, shall establish a study to
  8 15 analyze the projected financial effects of current and proposed
  8 16 United States environmental protection agency regulations and
  8 17 Iowa department of natural resources rules on Iowa cities over
  8 18 a ten=year period.
  8 19    2.  The study should include an analysis of projected
  8 20 financial costs of such regulations and rules on a hypothetical
  8 21 small Iowa community, medium=sized Iowa community, and large
  8 22 Iowa community.
  8 23    3.  The study shall be concluded by June 30, 2016, and a
  8 24 report shall be provided to the members of the general assembly
  8 25 and to the governor.
  8 26    Sec. 9.  EFFECTIVE DATE.  The section of this Act amending
  8 27 section 17A.7, subsection 2, takes effect July 1, 2017.
  8 28                           EXPLANATION
  8 29 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  8 30 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  8 31    This bill relates to the review of administrative rules and
  8 32 the rulemaking process.
  8 33    CITIZENS' ADVISORY COMMITTEE.  The bill requires that the
  8 34 administrative rules coordinator create a citizens' committee,
  8 35 to advise the administrative rules coordinator on rulemaking
  9  1 issues. The members of the committee shall not be paid a per
  9  2 diem but shall be reimbursed for travel expenses.
  9  3    RULEMAKING HEARINGS THROUGHOUT STATE.  The bill requires
  9  4 administrative agencies, to the extent practicable, to hold
  9  5 rulemaking hearings in varied locations throughout the state
  9  6 via the Iowa communications network or other electronic means
  9  7 and provides that a hearing must be held in a particular city
  9  8 or county when 25 interested persons from that city or county
  9  9 make the request.
  9 10    PRINCIPAL REASONS FOR AND AGAINST RULE.  The bill requires
  9 11 that every adopted rule must be accompanied by a concise
  9 12 statement of the principal reasons for and against the rule
  9 13 adopted. Under current law such a statement is only provided
  9 14 on request.
  9 15    JOBS IMPACT STATEMENTS.  The bill requires that every
  9 16 proposed rule under a notice of intended action or publication
  9 17 without notice contain a jobs impact statement which outlines
  9 18 the purpose and statutory authority of the rule and analyzes
  9 19 and sets out in detail the impact of the proposed rule on state
  9 20 agencies, local governments, the public, and the regulated
  9 21 entities, including regulated businesses and self=employed
  9 22 individuals affected by the rule. The statement must also
  9 23 determine whether a proposed rule would have a positive
  9 24 or negative impact on private sector jobs and employment
  9 25 opportunities.
  9 26    Commencing July 1, 2016, and every five years thereafter,
  9 27 each agency shall prepare a jobs impact statement for all of
  9 28 the agency's rules. The statement must be published in the
  9 29 Iowa administrative bulletin.
  9 30    As part of this requirement, an agency is required to
  9 31 takes steps to minimize the adverse impact on jobs and the
  9 32 development of new employment opportunities before proposing
  9 33 a rule.
  9 34    The administrative rules coordinator may waive the jobs
  9 35 impact statement requirement for emergency=filed rules or if
 10  1 unnecessary or impractical.
 10  2    NEGOTIATED RULEMAKING GROUPS.  If required by statute,
 10  3 this bill requires an agency to create an ad hoc negotiated
 10  4 rulemaking group to review draft rule proposals prior to
 10  5 commencing a rulemaking proceeding. Where a statute does not
 10  6 require this review, the bill allows an agency to create such
 10  7 a review group. Members are appointed by the agency and the
 10  8 composition must adequately represent a fair cross section of
 10  9 interests and opinions regarding the rule. Once such a group
 10 10 is created, the agency may only commence rulemaking after the
 10 11 group has considered the draft rule proposal in question. This
 10 12 provision is based on similar provisions found in the federal
 10 13 Administrative Procedures Act.
 10 14    FIVE=YEAR CYCLE OF AGENCY REVIEW OF RULES.  Current
 10 15 law requires that each state agency review all of its
 10 16 administrative rules on a five=year cycle. The bill provides
 10 17 additional procedures and criteria for such reviews.
 10 18    FEDERAL LAW IMPLEMENTATION.  The bill also provides that
 10 19 state implementation of a federal statute, regulation,
 10 20 or policy by a state agency shall not exceed the specific
 10 21 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or
 10 22 policy, except as specifically allowed by state law. Any
 10 23 portion of a state rule or policy that implements a federal
 10 24 statute, regulation, or policy and that exceeds the specific
 10 25 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or policy is
 10 26 automatically superseded by the specific requirements of that
 10 27 federal statute, regulation, or policy.
 10 28    ENVIRONMENTAL RULES STUDY.  The bill provides that the
 10 29 legislative council, in consultation with the department of
 10 30 natural resources, shall establish a study to analyze the
 10 31 projected financial effects of current and proposed United
 10 32 States environmental protection agency regulations and Iowa
 10 33 department of natural resources rules on Iowa cities over a
 10 34 10=year period. The report of the study must be completed by
 10 35 June 30, 2016.
 11  1 EFFECTIVE DATE.  The provision of the bill relating to state
 11  2 agency review of administrative rules on a five=year cycle
 11  3 takes effect July 1, 2017.
       LSB 1809XS (3) 86
       je/rj
  8 11 of that federal statute, regulation, or policy.
  8 12    Sec. 8.  ENVIRONMENTAL REGULATION STUDY.
  8 13    1.  The legislative council, in consultation with the
  8 14 department of natural resources, shall establish a study to
  8 15 analyze the projected financial effects of current and proposed
  8 16 United States environmental protection agency regulations and
  8 17 Iowa department of natural resources rules on Iowa cities over
  8 18 a ten=year period.
  8 19    2.  The study should include an analysis of projected
  8 20 financial costs of such regulations and rules on a hypothetical
  8 21 small Iowa community, medium=sized Iowa community, and large
  8 22 Iowa community.
  8 23    3.  The study shall be concluded by June 30, 2016, and a
  8 24 report shall be provided to the members of the general assembly
  8 25 and to the governor.
  8 26    Sec. 9.  EFFECTIVE DATE.  The section of this Act amending
  8 27 section 17A.7, subsection 2, takes effect July 1, 2017.

  9  2 diem but shall be reimbursed for travel expenses.

  9  4 administrative agencies, to the extent practicable, to hold
  9  5 rulemaking hearings in varied locations throughout the state
  9  6 via the Iowa communications network or other electronic means
  9  7 and provides that a hearing must be held in a particular city
  9  8 or county when 25 interested persons from that city or county
  9  9 make the request.
  9 10    PRINCIPAL REASONS FOR AND AGAINST RULE.  The bill requires
  9 11 that every adopted rule must be accompanied by a concise
  9 12 statement of the principal reasons for and against the rule
  9 13 adopted. Under current law such a statement is only provided
  9 14 on request.
  9 15    JOBS IMPACT STATEMENTS.  The bill requires that every
  9 16 proposed rule under a notice of intended action or publication
  9 17 without notice contain a jobs impact statement which outlines
  9 18 the purpose and statutory authority of the rule and analyzes
  9 19 and sets out in detail the impact of the proposed rule on state
  9 20 agencies, local governments, the public, and the regulated
  9 21 entities, including regulated businesses and self=employed
  9 22 individuals affected by the rule. The statement must also
  9 23 determine whether a proposed rule would have a positive
  9 24 or negative impact on private sector jobs and employment
  9 25 opportunities.
  9 26    Commencing July 1, 2016, and every five years thereafter,
  9 27 each agency shall prepare a jobs impact statement for all of
  9 28 the agency's rules. The statement must be published in the
  9 29 Iowa administrative bulletin.
  9 30    As part of this requirement, an agency is required to
  9 31 takes steps to minimize the adverse impact on jobs and the
  9 32 development of new employment opportunities before proposing
  9 33 a rule.
  9 34    The administrative rules coordinator may waive the jobs
  9 35 impact statement requirement for emergency=filed rules or if
 10  1 unnecessary or impractical.
 10  2    NEGOTIATED RULEMAKING GROUPS.  If required by statute,
 10  3 this bill requires an agency to create an ad hoc negotiated
 10  4 rulemaking group to review draft rule proposals prior to
 10  5 commencing a rulemaking proceeding. Where a statute does not
 10  6 require this review, the bill allows an agency to create such
 10  7 a review group. Members are appointed by the agency and the
 10  8 composition must adequately represent a fair cross section of
 10  9 interests and opinions regarding the rule. Once such a group
 10 10 is created, the agency may only commence rulemaking after the
 10 11 group has considered the draft rule proposal in question. This
 10 12 provision is based on similar provisions found in the federal
 10 13 Administrative Procedures Act.
 10 14    FIVE=YEAR CYCLE OF AGENCY REVIEW OF RULES.  Current
 10 15 law requires that each state agency review all of its
 10 16 administrative rules on a five=year cycle. The bill provides
 10 17 additional procedures and criteria for such reviews.
 10 18    FEDERAL LAW IMPLEMENTATION.  The bill also provides that
 10 19 state implementation of a federal statute, regulation,
 10 20 or policy by a state agency shall not exceed the specific
 10 21 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or
 10 22 policy, except as specifically allowed by state law. Any
 10 23 portion of a state rule or policy that implements a federal
 10 24 statute, regulation, or policy and that exceeds the specific
 10 25 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or policy is
 10 26 automatically superseded by the specific requirements of that
 10 27 federal statute, regulation, or policy.
 10 28    ENVIRONMENTAL RULES STUDY.  The bill provides that the
 10 29 legislative council, in consultation with the department of
 10 30 natural resources, shall establish a study to analyze the
 10 31 projected financial effects of current and proposed United
 10 32 States environmental protection agency regulations and Iowa
 10 33 department of natural resources rules on Iowa cities over a
 10 34 10=year period. The report of the study must be completed by
 10 35 June 30, 2016.
 11  1 EFFECTIVE DATE.  The provision of the bill relating to state
 11  2 agency review of administrative rules on a five=year cycle
 11  3 takes effect July 1, 2017.
       LSB 1809XS (3) 86
       je/rj
  8 16 United States environmental protection agency regulations and
  8 17 Iowa department of natural resources rules on Iowa cities over
  8 18 a ten=year period.
  8 19    2.  The study should include an analysis of projected
  8 20 financial costs of such regulations and rules on a hypothetical
  8 21 small Iowa community, medium=sized Iowa community, and large
  8 22 Iowa community.
  8 23    3.  The study shall be concluded by June 30, 2016, and a
  8 24 report shall be provided to the members of the general assembly
  8 25 and to the governor.
  8 26    Sec. 9.  EFFECTIVE DATE.  The section of this Act amending
  8 27 section 17A.7, subsection 2, takes effect July 1, 2017.

  8 21 small Iowa community, medium=sized Iowa community, and large
  8 22 Iowa community.
  8 23    3.  The study shall be concluded by June 30, 2016, and a
  8 24 report shall be provided to the members of the general assembly
  8 25 and to the governor.
  8 26    Sec. 9.  EFFECTIVE DATE.  The section of this Act amending
  8 27 section 17A.7, subsection 2, takes effect July 1, 2017.
  8 28                           EXPLANATION
  8 29 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  8 30 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  8 31    This bill relates to the review of administrative rules and
  8 32 the rulemaking process.
  8 33    CITIZENS' ADVISORY COMMITTEE.  The bill requires that the
  8 34 administrative rules coordinator create a citizens' committee,
  8 35 to advise the administrative rules coordinator on rulemaking
  9  1 issues. The members of the committee shall not be paid a per
  9  2 diem but shall be reimbursed for travel expenses.
  9  3    RULEMAKING HEARINGS THROUGHOUT STATE.  The bill requires
  9  4 administrative agencies, to the extent practicable, to hold
  9  5 rulemaking hearings in varied locations throughout the state
  9  6 via the Iowa communications network or other electronic means
  9  7 and provides that a hearing must be held in a particular city
  9  8 or county when 25 interested persons from that city or county
  9  9 make the request.
  9 10    PRINCIPAL REASONS FOR AND AGAINST RULE.  The bill requires
  9 11 that every adopted rule must be accompanied by a concise
  9 12 statement of the principal reasons for and against the rule
  9 13 adopted. Under current law such a statement is only provided
  9 14 on request.
  9 15    JOBS IMPACT STATEMENTS.  The bill requires that every
  9 16 proposed rule under a notice of intended action or publication
  9 17 without notice contain a jobs impact statement which outlines
  9 18 the purpose and statutory authority of the rule and analyzes
  9 19 and sets out in detail the impact of the proposed rule on state
  9 20 agencies, local governments, the public, and the regulated
  9 21 entities, including regulated businesses and self=employed
  9 22 individuals affected by the rule. The statement must also
  9 23 determine whether a proposed rule would have a positive
  9 24 or negative impact on private sector jobs and employment
  9 25 opportunities.
  9 26    Commencing July 1, 2016, and every five years thereafter,
  9 27 each agency shall prepare a jobs impact statement for all of
  9 28 the agency's rules. The statement must be published in the
  9 29 Iowa administrative bulletin.
  9 30    As part of this requirement, an agency is required to
  9 31 takes steps to minimize the adverse impact on jobs and the
  9 32 development of new employment opportunities before proposing
  9 33 a rule.
  9 34    The administrative rules coordinator may waive the jobs
  9 35 impact statement requirement for emergency=filed rules or if
 10  1 unnecessary or impractical.
 10  2    NEGOTIATED RULEMAKING GROUPS.  If required by statute,
 10  3 this bill requires an agency to create an ad hoc negotiated
 10  4 rulemaking group to review draft rule proposals prior to
 10  5 commencing a rulemaking proceeding. Where a statute does not
 10  6 require this review, the bill allows an agency to create such
 10  7 a review group. Members are appointed by the agency and the
 10  8 composition must adequately represent a fair cross section of
 10  9 interests and opinions regarding the rule. Once such a group
 10 10 is created, the agency may only commence rulemaking after the
 10 11 group has considered the draft rule proposal in question. This
 10 12 provision is based on similar provisions found in the federal
 10 13 Administrative Procedures Act.
 10 14    FIVE=YEAR CYCLE OF AGENCY REVIEW OF RULES.  Current
 10 15 law requires that each state agency review all of its
 10 16 administrative rules on a five=year cycle. The bill provides
 10 17 additional procedures and criteria for such reviews.
 10 18    FEDERAL LAW IMPLEMENTATION.  The bill also provides that
 10 19 state implementation of a federal statute, regulation,
 10 20 or policy by a state agency shall not exceed the specific
 10 21 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or
 10 22 policy, except as specifically allowed by state law. Any
 10 23 portion of a state rule or policy that implements a federal
 10 24 statute, regulation, or policy and that exceeds the specific
 10 25 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or policy is
 10 26 automatically superseded by the specific requirements of that
 10 27 federal statute, regulation, or policy.
 10 28    ENVIRONMENTAL RULES STUDY.  The bill provides that the
 10 29 legislative council, in consultation with the department of
 10 30 natural resources, shall establish a study to analyze the
 10 31 projected financial effects of current and proposed United
 10 32 States environmental protection agency regulations and Iowa
 10 33 department of natural resources rules on Iowa cities over a
 10 34 10=year period. The report of the study must be completed by
 10 35 June 30, 2016.
 11  1 EFFECTIVE DATE.  The provision of the bill relating to state
 11  2 agency review of administrative rules on a five=year cycle
 11  3 takes effect July 1, 2017.
       LSB 1809XS (3) 86
       je/rj
  8 22 Iowa community.
  8 23    3.  The study shall be concluded by June 30, 2016, and a
  8 24 report shall be provided to the members of the general assembly
  8 25 and to the governor.
  8 26    Sec. 9.  EFFECTIVE DATE.  The section of this Act amending
  8 27 section 17A.7, subsection 2, takes effect July 1, 2017.

  8 35 to advise the administrative rules coordinator on rulemaking
  9  1 issues. The members of the committee shall not be paid a per
  9  2 diem but shall be reimbursed for travel expenses.
  9  3    RULEMAKING HEARINGS THROUGHOUT STATE.  The bill requires
  9  4 administrative agencies, to the extent practicable, to hold
  9  5 rulemaking hearings in varied locations throughout the state
  9  6 via the Iowa communications network or other electronic means
  9  7 and provides that a hearing must be held in a particular city
  9  8 or county when 25 interested persons from that city or county
  9  9 make the request.
  9 10    PRINCIPAL REASONS FOR AND AGAINST RULE.  The bill requires
  9 11 that every adopted rule must be accompanied by a concise
  9 12 statement of the principal reasons for and against the rule
  9 13 adopted. Under current law such a statement is only provided
  9 14 on request.
  9 15    JOBS IMPACT STATEMENTS.  The bill requires that every
  9 16 proposed rule under a notice of intended action or publication
  9 17 without notice contain a jobs impact statement which outlines
  9 18 the purpose and statutory authority of the rule and analyzes
  9 19 and sets out in detail the impact of the proposed rule on state
  9 20 agencies, local governments, the public, and the regulated
  9 21 entities, including regulated businesses and self=employed
  9 22 individuals affected by the rule. The statement must also
  9 23 determine whether a proposed rule would have a positive
  9 24 or negative impact on private sector jobs and employment
  9 25 opportunities.
  9 26    Commencing July 1, 2016, and every five years thereafter,
  9 27 each agency shall prepare a jobs impact statement for all of
  9 28 the agency's rules. The statement must be published in the
  9 29 Iowa administrative bulletin.
  9 30    As part of this requirement, an agency is required to
  9 31 takes steps to minimize the adverse impact on jobs and the
  9 32 development of new employment opportunities before proposing
  9 33 a rule.
  9 34    The administrative rules coordinator may waive the jobs
  9 35 impact statement requirement for emergency=filed rules or if
 10  1 unnecessary or impractical.
 10  2    NEGOTIATED RULEMAKING GROUPS.  If required by statute,
 10  3 this bill requires an agency to create an ad hoc negotiated
 10  4 rulemaking group to review draft rule proposals prior to
 10  5 commencing a rulemaking proceeding. Where a statute does not
 10  6 require this review, the bill allows an agency to create such
 10  7 a review group. Members are appointed by the agency and the
 10  8 composition must adequately represent a fair cross section of
 10  9 interests and opinions regarding the rule. Once such a group
 10 10 is created, the agency may only commence rulemaking after the
 10 11 group has considered the draft rule proposal in question. This
 10 12 provision is based on similar provisions found in the federal
 10 13 Administrative Procedures Act.
 10 14    FIVE=YEAR CYCLE OF AGENCY REVIEW OF RULES.  Current
 10 15 law requires that each state agency review all of its
 10 16 administrative rules on a five=year cycle. The bill provides
 10 17 additional procedures and criteria for such reviews.
 10 18    FEDERAL LAW IMPLEMENTATION.  The bill also provides that
 10 19 state implementation of a federal statute, regulation,
 10 20 or policy by a state agency shall not exceed the specific
 10 21 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or
 10 22 policy, except as specifically allowed by state law. Any
 10 23 portion of a state rule or policy that implements a federal
 10 24 statute, regulation, or policy and that exceeds the specific
 10 25 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or policy is
 10 26 automatically superseded by the specific requirements of that
 10 27 federal statute, regulation, or policy.
 10 28    ENVIRONMENTAL RULES STUDY.  The bill provides that the
 10 29 legislative council, in consultation with the department of
 10 30 natural resources, shall establish a study to analyze the
 10 31 projected financial effects of current and proposed United
 10 32 States environmental protection agency regulations and Iowa
 10 33 department of natural resources rules on Iowa cities over a
 10 34 10=year period. The report of the study must be completed by
 10 35 June 30, 2016.
 11  1 EFFECTIVE DATE.  The provision of the bill relating to state
 11  2 agency review of administrative rules on a five=year cycle
 11  3 takes effect July 1, 2017.
       LSB 1809XS (3) 86
       je/rj

 10 22 policy, except as specifically allowed by state law. Any
 10 23 portion of a state rule or policy that implements a federal
 10 24 statute, regulation, or policy and that exceeds the specific
 10 25 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or policy is
 10 26 automatically superseded by the specific requirements of that
 10 27 federal statute, regulation, or policy.
 10 28    ENVIRONMENTAL RULES STUDY.  The bill provides that the
 10 29 legislative council, in consultation with the department of
 10 30 natural resources, shall establish a study to analyze the
 10 31 projected financial effects of current and proposed United
 10 32 States environmental protection agency regulations and Iowa
 10 33 department of natural resources rules on Iowa cities over a
 10 34 10=year period. The report of the study must be completed by
 10 35 June 30, 2016.
 11  1 EFFECTIVE DATE.  The provision of the bill relating to state
 11  2 agency review of administrative rules on a five=year cycle
 11  3 takes effect July 1, 2017.
       LSB 1809XS (3) 86
       je/rj
  8 34 administrative rules coordinator create a citizens' committee,
  8 35 to advise the administrative rules coordinator on rulemaking
  9  1 issues. The members of the committee shall not be paid a per
  9  2 diem but shall be reimbursed for travel expenses.
  9  3    RULEMAKING HEARINGS THROUGHOUT STATE.  The bill requires
  9  4 administrative agencies, to the extent practicable, to hold
  9  5 rulemaking hearings in varied locations throughout the state
  9  6 via the Iowa communications network or other electronic means
  9  7 and provides that a hearing must be held in a particular city
  9  8 or county when 25 interested persons from that city or county
  9  9 make the request.
  9 10    PRINCIPAL REASONS FOR AND AGAINST RULE.  The bill requires
  9 11 that every adopted rule must be accompanied by a concise
  9 12 statement of the principal reasons for and against the rule
  9 13 adopted. Under current law such a statement is only provided
  9 14 on request.
  9 15    JOBS IMPACT STATEMENTS.  The bill requires that every
  9 16 proposed rule under a notice of intended action or publication
  9 17 without notice contain a jobs impact statement which outlines
  9 18 the purpose and statutory authority of the rule and analyzes
  9 19 and sets out in detail the impact of the proposed rule on state
  9 20 agencies, local governments, the public, and the regulated
  9 21 entities, including regulated businesses and self=employed
  9 22 individuals affected by the rule. The statement must also
  9 23 determine whether a proposed rule would have a positive
  9 24 or negative impact on private sector jobs and employment
  9 25 opportunities.
  9 26    Commencing July 1, 2016, and every five years thereafter,
  9 27 each agency shall prepare a jobs impact statement for all of
  9 28 the agency's rules. The statement must be published in the
  9 29 Iowa administrative bulletin.
  9 30    As part of this requirement, an agency is required to
  9 31 takes steps to minimize the adverse impact on jobs and the
  9 32 development of new employment opportunities before proposing
  9 33 a rule.
  9 34    The administrative rules coordinator may waive the jobs
  9 35 impact statement requirement for emergency=filed rules or if
 10  1 unnecessary or impractical.
 10  2    NEGOTIATED RULEMAKING GROUPS.  If required by statute,
 10  3 this bill requires an agency to create an ad hoc negotiated
 10  4 rulemaking group to review draft rule proposals prior to
 10  5 commencing a rulemaking proceeding. Where a statute does not
 10  6 require this review, the bill allows an agency to create such
 10  7 a review group. Members are appointed by the agency and the
 10  8 composition must adequately represent a fair cross section of
 10  9 interests and opinions regarding the rule. Once such a group
 10 10 is created, the agency may only commence rulemaking after the
 10 11 group has considered the draft rule proposal in question. This
 10 12 provision is based on similar provisions found in the federal
 10 13 Administrative Procedures Act.
 10 14    FIVE=YEAR CYCLE OF AGENCY REVIEW OF RULES.  Current
 10 15 law requires that each state agency review all of its
 10 16 administrative rules on a five=year cycle. The bill provides
 10 17 additional procedures and criteria for such reviews.
 10 18    FEDERAL LAW IMPLEMENTATION.  The bill also provides that
 10 19 state implementation of a federal statute, regulation,
 10 20 or policy by a state agency shall not exceed the specific
 10 21 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or
 10 22 policy, except as specifically allowed by state law. Any
 10 23 portion of a state rule or policy that implements a federal
 10 24 statute, regulation, or policy and that exceeds the specific
 10 25 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or policy is
 10 26 automatically superseded by the specific requirements of that
 10 27 federal statute, regulation, or policy.
 10 28    ENVIRONMENTAL RULES STUDY.  The bill provides that the
 10 29 legislative council, in consultation with the department of
 10 30 natural resources, shall establish a study to analyze the
 10 31 projected financial effects of current and proposed United
 10 32 States environmental protection agency regulations and Iowa
 10 33 department of natural resources rules on Iowa cities over a
 10 34 10=year period. The report of the study must be completed by
 10 35 June 30, 2016.
 11  1 EFFECTIVE DATE.  The provision of the bill relating to state
 11  2 agency review of administrative rules on a five=year cycle
 11  3 takes effect July 1, 2017.

  9 13 adopted. Under current law such a statement is only provided
  9 14 on request.
  9 15    JOBS IMPACT STATEMENTS.  The bill requires that every
  9 16 proposed rule under a notice of intended action or publication
  9 17 without notice contain a jobs impact statement which outlines
  9 18 the purpose and statutory authority of the rule and analyzes
  9 19 and sets out in detail the impact of the proposed rule on state
  9 20 agencies, local governments, the public, and the regulated
  9 21 entities, including regulated businesses and self=employed
  9 22 individuals affected by the rule. The statement must also
  9 23 determine whether a proposed rule would have a positive
  9 24 or negative impact on private sector jobs and employment
  9 25 opportunities.
  9 26    Commencing July 1, 2016, and every five years thereafter,
  9 27 each agency shall prepare a jobs impact statement for all of
  9 28 the agency's rules. The statement must be published in the
  9 29 Iowa administrative bulletin.
  9 30    As part of this requirement, an agency is required to
  9 31 takes steps to minimize the adverse impact on jobs and the
  9 32 development of new employment opportunities before proposing
  9 33 a rule.
  9 34    The administrative rules coordinator may waive the jobs
  9 35 impact statement requirement for emergency=filed rules or if
 10  1 unnecessary or impractical.
 10  2    NEGOTIATED RULEMAKING GROUPS.  If required by statute,
 10  3 this bill requires an agency to create an ad hoc negotiated
 10  4 rulemaking group to review draft rule proposals prior to
 10  5 commencing a rulemaking proceeding. Where a statute does not
 10  6 require this review, the bill allows an agency to create such
 10  7 a review group. Members are appointed by the agency and the
 10  8 composition must adequately represent a fair cross section of
 10  9 interests and opinions regarding the rule. Once such a group
 10 10 is created, the agency may only commence rulemaking after the
 10 11 group has considered the draft rule proposal in question. This
 10 12 provision is based on similar provisions found in the federal
 10 13 Administrative Procedures Act.
 10 14    FIVE=YEAR CYCLE OF AGENCY REVIEW OF RULES.  Current
 10 15 law requires that each state agency review all of its
 10 16 administrative rules on a five=year cycle. The bill provides
 10 17 additional procedures and criteria for such reviews.
 10 18    FEDERAL LAW IMPLEMENTATION.  The bill also provides that
 10 19 state implementation of a federal statute, regulation,
 10 20 or policy by a state agency shall not exceed the specific
 10 21 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or
 10 22 policy, except as specifically allowed by state law. Any
 10 23 portion of a state rule or policy that implements a federal
 10 24 statute, regulation, or policy and that exceeds the specific
 10 25 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or policy is
 10 26 automatically superseded by the specific requirements of that
 10 27 federal statute, regulation, or policy.
 10 28    ENVIRONMENTAL RULES STUDY.  The bill provides that the
 10 29 legislative council, in consultation with the department of
 10 30 natural resources, shall establish a study to analyze the
 10 31 projected financial effects of current and proposed United
 10 32 States environmental protection agency regulations and Iowa
 10 33 department of natural resources rules on Iowa cities over a
 10 34 10=year period. The report of the study must be completed by
 10 35 June 30, 2016.
 11  1 EFFECTIVE DATE.  The provision of the bill relating to state
 11  2 agency review of administrative rules on a five=year cycle
 11  3 takes effect July 1, 2017.
       LSB 1809XS (3) 86

  9  7 and provides that a hearing must be held in a particular city
  9  8 or county when 25 interested persons from that city or county
  9  9 make the request.
