 10  7 a review group. Members are appointed by the agency and the
 10  8 composition must adequately represent a fair cross section of
 10  9 interests and opinions regarding the rule. Once such a group
 10 10 is created, the agency may only commence rulemaking after the
 10 11 group has considered the draft rule proposal in question. This
 10 12 provision is based on similar provisions found in the federal
 10 13 Administrative Procedures Act.
 10 14    FIVE=YEAR CYCLE OF AGENCY REVIEW OF RULES.  Current
 10 15 law requires that each state agency review all of its
 10 16 administrative rules on a five=year cycle. The bill provides
 10 17 additional procedures and criteria for such reviews.
 10 18    FEDERAL LAW IMPLEMENTATION.  The bill also provides that
 10 19 state implementation of a federal statute, regulation,
 10 20 or policy by a state agency shall not exceed the specific
 10 21 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or
 10 22 policy, except as specifically allowed by state law. Any
 10 23 portion of a state rule or policy that implements a federal
 10 24 statute, regulation, or policy and that exceeds the specific
 10 25 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or policy is
 10 26 automatically superseded by the specific requirements of that
 10 27 federal statute, regulation, or policy.
 10 28    ENVIRONMENTAL RULES STUDY.  The bill provides that the
 10 29 legislative council, in consultation with the department of
 10 30 natural resources, shall establish a study to analyze the
 10 31 projected financial effects of current and proposed United
 10 32 States environmental protection agency regulations and Iowa
 10 33 department of natural resources rules on Iowa cities over a
 10 34 10=year period. The report of the study must be completed by
 10 35 June 30, 2016.
 11  1 EFFECTIVE DATE.  The provision of the bill relating to state
 11  2 agency review of administrative rules on a five=year cycle
 11  3 takes effect July 1, 2017.
       LSB 1809XS (3) 86
       je/rj
  9 15    JOBS IMPACT STATEMENTS.  The bill requires that every
  9 16 proposed rule under a notice of intended action or publication
  9 17 without notice contain a jobs impact statement which outlines
  9 18 the purpose and statutory authority of the rule and analyzes
  9 19 and sets out in detail the impact of the proposed rule on state
  9 20 agencies, local governments, the public, and the regulated
  9 21 entities, including regulated businesses and self=employed
  9 22 individuals affected by the rule. The statement must also
  9 23 determine whether a proposed rule would have a positive
  9 24 or negative impact on private sector jobs and employment
  9 25 opportunities.
  9 26    Commencing July 1, 2016, and every five years thereafter,
  9 27 each agency shall prepare a jobs impact statement for all of
  9 28 the agency's rules. The statement must be published in the
  9 29 Iowa administrative bulletin.
  9 30    As part of this requirement, an agency is required to
  9 31 takes steps to minimize the adverse impact on jobs and the
  9 32 development of new employment opportunities before proposing
  9 33 a rule.
  9 34    The administrative rules coordinator may waive the jobs
  9 35 impact statement requirement for emergency=filed rules or if
 10  1 unnecessary or impractical.
 10  2    NEGOTIATED RULEMAKING GROUPS.  If required by statute,
 10  3 this bill requires an agency to create an ad hoc negotiated
 10  4 rulemaking group to review draft rule proposals prior to
 10  5 commencing a rulemaking proceeding. Where a statute does not
 10  6 require this review, the bill allows an agency to create such
 10  7 a review group. Members are appointed by the agency and the
 10  8 composition must adequately represent a fair cross section of
 10  9 interests and opinions regarding the rule. Once such a group
 10 10 is created, the agency may only commence rulemaking after the
 10 11 group has considered the draft rule proposal in question. This
 10 12 provision is based on similar provisions found in the federal
 10 13 Administrative Procedures Act.
 10 14    FIVE=YEAR CYCLE OF AGENCY REVIEW OF RULES.  Current
 10 15 law requires that each state agency review all of its
 10 16 administrative rules on a five=year cycle. The bill provides
 10 17 additional procedures and criteria for such reviews.
 10 18    FEDERAL LAW IMPLEMENTATION.  The bill also provides that
 10 19 state implementation of a federal statute, regulation,

 10 24 statute, regulation, or policy and that exceeds the specific
 10 25 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or policy is

 10 27 federal statute, regulation, or policy.

  9 34    The administrative rules coordinator may waive the jobs
  9 35 impact statement requirement for emergency=filed rules or if
 10  1 unnecessary or impractical.
 10  2    NEGOTIATED RULEMAKING GROUPS.  If required by statute,
 10  3 this bill requires an agency to create an ad hoc negotiated
 10  4 rulemaking group to review draft rule proposals prior to
 10  5 commencing a rulemaking proceeding. Where a statute does not
 10  6 require this review, the bill allows an agency to create such
 10  7 a review group. Members are appointed by the agency and the
 10  8 composition must adequately represent a fair cross section of
 10  9 interests and opinions regarding the rule. Once such a group
 10 10 is created, the agency may only commence rulemaking after the
 10 11 group has considered the draft rule proposal in question. This
 10 12 provision is based on similar provisions found in the federal
 10 13 Administrative Procedures Act.
 10 14    FIVE=YEAR CYCLE OF AGENCY REVIEW OF RULES.  Current
 10 15 law requires that each state agency review all of its
 10 16 administrative rules on a five=year cycle. The bill provides
 10 17 additional procedures and criteria for such reviews.
 10 18    FEDERAL LAW IMPLEMENTATION.  The bill also provides that
 10 19 state implementation of a federal statute, regulation,
 10 20 or policy by a state agency shall not exceed the specific
 10 21 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or
 10 22 policy, except as specifically allowed by state law. Any
 10 23 portion of a state rule or policy that implements a federal
 10 24 statute, regulation, or policy and that exceeds the specific
 10 25 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or policy is
 10 26 automatically superseded by the specific requirements of that
 10 27 federal statute, regulation, or policy.
 10 28    ENVIRONMENTAL RULES STUDY.  The bill provides that the
 10 29 legislative council, in consultation with the department of
 10 30 natural resources, shall establish a study to analyze the
 10 31 projected financial effects of current and proposed United
 10 32 States environmental protection agency regulations and Iowa
 10 33 department of natural resources rules on Iowa cities over a
 10 34 10=year period. The report of the study must be completed by
 10 35 June 30, 2016.
 11  1 EFFECTIVE DATE.  The provision of the bill relating to state
 11  2 agency review of administrative rules on a five=year cycle
 11  3 takes effect July 1, 2017.
       LSB 1809XS (3) 86
       je/rj
  9 25 opportunities.
  9 26    Commencing July 1, 2016, and every five years thereafter,
  9 27 each agency shall prepare a jobs impact statement for all of
  9 28 the agency's rules. The statement must be published in the
  9 29 Iowa administrative bulletin.
  9 30    As part of this requirement, an agency is required to
  9 31 takes steps to minimize the adverse impact on jobs and the
  9 32 development of new employment opportunities before proposing
  9 33 a rule.

  9 35 impact statement requirement for emergency=filed rules or if

 10  7 a review group. Members are appointed by the agency and the
 10  8 composition must adequately represent a fair cross section of
 10  9 interests and opinions regarding the rule. Once such a group
 10 10 is created, the agency may only commence rulemaking after the
 10 11 group has considered the draft rule proposal in question. This
 10 12 provision is based on similar provisions found in the federal
 10 13 Administrative Procedures Act.
 10 14    FIVE=YEAR CYCLE OF AGENCY REVIEW OF RULES.  Current
 10 15 law requires that each state agency review all of its
 10 16 administrative rules on a five=year cycle. The bill provides
 10 17 additional procedures and criteria for such reviews.
 10 18    FEDERAL LAW IMPLEMENTATION.  The bill also provides that
 10 19 state implementation of a federal statute, regulation,
 10 20 or policy by a state agency shall not exceed the specific
 10 21 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or
 10 22 policy, except as specifically allowed by state law. Any
 10 23 portion of a state rule or policy that implements a federal
 10 24 statute, regulation, or policy and that exceeds the specific
 10 25 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or policy is
 10 26 automatically superseded by the specific requirements of that
 10 27 federal statute, regulation, or policy.
 10 28    ENVIRONMENTAL RULES STUDY.  The bill provides that the
 10 29 legislative council, in consultation with the department of
 10 30 natural resources, shall establish a study to analyze the
 10 31 projected financial effects of current and proposed United
 10 32 States environmental protection agency regulations and Iowa
 10 33 department of natural resources rules on Iowa cities over a
 10 34 10=year period. The report of the study must be completed by
 10 35 June 30, 2016.
 11  1 EFFECTIVE DATE.  The provision of the bill relating to state
 11  2 agency review of administrative rules on a five=year cycle
 11  3 takes effect July 1, 2017.
       LSB 1809XS (3) 86
       je/rj
 10  2    NEGOTIATED RULEMAKING GROUPS.  If required by statute,
 10  3 this bill requires an agency to create an ad hoc negotiated
 10  4 rulemaking group to review draft rule proposals prior to
 10  5 commencing a rulemaking proceeding. Where a statute does not
 10  6 require this review, the bill allows an agency to create such
 10  7 a review group. Members are appointed by the agency and the
 10  8 composition must adequately represent a fair cross section of
 10  9 interests and opinions regarding the rule. Once such a group
 10 10 is created, the agency may only commence rulemaking after the
 10 11 group has considered the draft rule proposal in question. This
 10 12 provision is based on similar provisions found in the federal
 10 13 Administrative Procedures Act.
 10 14    FIVE=YEAR CYCLE OF AGENCY REVIEW OF RULES.  Current
 10 15 law requires that each state agency review all of its
 10 16 administrative rules on a five=year cycle. The bill provides
 10 17 additional procedures and criteria for such reviews.

 10 19 state implementation of a federal statute, regulation,
 10 20 or policy by a state agency shall not exceed the specific
 10 21 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or
 10 22 policy, except as specifically allowed by state law. Any
 10 23 portion of a state rule or policy that implements a federal
 10 24 statute, regulation, or policy and that exceeds the specific
 10 25 requirements of the federal statute, regulation, or policy is
 10 26 automatically superseded by the specific requirements of that
 10 27 federal statute, regulation, or policy.
 10 28    ENVIRONMENTAL RULES STUDY.  The bill provides that the
 10 29 legislative council, in consultation with the department of
 10 30 natural resources, shall establish a study to analyze the
 10 31 projected financial effects of current and proposed United
 10 32 States environmental protection agency regulations and Iowa
 10 33 department of natural resources rules on Iowa cities over a
 10 34 10=year period. The report of the study must be completed by
 10 35 June 30, 2016.
